<resp>None<//resp>< review>
In Fresno for the first time and decided to checkout Golden Grill. I am always looking for good Lebanese food. Placed an order to go for the mixed grilled kebans with hummus and the fattous salad. Hummus is super creamy. The balance of hummus to bread is 80 20. No worries used my kebabs to scoop up the rest.

Each kebab full of flavor. Also the beef kebab was cooked perfectly of between medium and medium rare. I have had some at other places that cook the beef too long. Not here, just perfectly balanced. The chicken was not over cooked either. Still juicy. Also the kafta was cooked great too. Just how all of these were done you can see they know the right timeline to cook each with overcooking. The is key to great kebabs.

I will be back the next time I am in Fresno.</review>

<Text>Just ate there. Having the option of white or brown rice or a salad mix is nice. They don't use "the" authentic rice you'd get in Hawaii, which is/was Hinode, but it's close. The shoyu ahi side of my combo bowl - with avocado for free - but the shoyu salmon was disgusting. Fishy-smelling, low-grade, salmon-colored "stuff". I actually got a partial refund (the guy asked if I wanted my money back and I said since I'd eaten some about half back would be fair) because the salmon was gross.

The owners are nice people but some things don't translate well. I'd not expect excellent Mexican food back in Hawaii, for instance.

So if you go, avoid the salmon, get the avocado add-on if you like that sort of thing because it, or a number of others, are included in the price, keep in mind they've got shoyu and furikake etc there to put on yourself, and yeah, the servings are decent.< /Text>< Pictures>

If there is one thing on the menu to get, it is their acai bowls. Truly authentic and delicious! I also tried their Shoyu Ahi Tuna bowl and enjoyed it - it was a little more bitter than I liked (the tuna had a stronger flavor) but it was definitely very fresh. I can't speak to other reviews but you could tell this was definitely a Latin American twist on poke and I really enjoyed it. Is everything a bit pricey? Yes, but the acai bowl is well worth it!
PS - the folks running this place are really awesome - a really great experience!</Review>

< Review>
We were super excited when we bought our home in Wildomar, as it's only 1 mile or so from Angelo's! After our first visit we were hooked. The owners are very active in their business and it's nice to go and be remembered whenever we go. Since the pandemic hit, they have done an amazing job of keeping their dependable business going. We have ordered there nearly 1x a week since the pandemic hit. Our orders are always exactly what we asked for and extremely consistent. I am originally from the Boston area and have VERY high standards for Italian food and especially pizza. Angelo's is our go-to for pizza and pasta. Everything is made to order and the brick oven pizza is a MUST. It is our absolute favorite in Temecula Valley - we almost want to keep them all to ourselves, but they deserve to be internationally known. We also love that they have gluten-free and cauliflower crust options. Grazie to Angelo and the entire staff. We appreciate how hard you're working to provide excellent service during a difficult time.</Review>

<UserId.>111156317340652306212<//UserId.><name>John Concialdi</name>< Date>
1577100543265<//Date>
<rate>5< /rate>< text>
OMFG, we found a real Italian restaurant in Wildomar. This was my 1st time there and my girlfriend tried it during the week. I'm always a little skeptical about Italian restaurants because being Italian, I grew up on mom's cooking which of course was amazing, so the benchmark is quite high. Turns out Angelo is from Sicily and the guy has some serious talent.
I had a pasta carbonara made in his interpretation which used a robust thick pancetta. It is a bit richer than Roman carbonara and seriously good. BTW we have been all over Italy and Sicily and I make it a point to test restaurants with carbonara because of the huge variety recipes. Angelo's is top notch.
My gf had the "1874" pizza which is right up there with Eatalian in Gardena. That is saying g something because they are the standard of pizza IMO. Angelo's crust is slightly thicker than milanese pizza but that is the Sicilian way. We often compare pizza to a little shop we ran into in Positano and again Angelo's holds up to the test.
Service was sublime, out waitress knew her way around the menu and she was attentive and very polite. As a nice touch, we met a family there and the grandmother is from northern Italy and we had a fantastic conversation about Italian food.
Go here, it is yet another gem in Wildomar,</text>

< Text>
EXCELLENT food!  Ended up in Wildomar going with my husband on a solar job. While waiting i had my toes done at Vies( excellent) and was told Angelos across the way was excellent pizza! Service was friendly and attentive. All meals served with this fabulous flatbread! Bread was delish, but the kitchen took forever getting it out. When you pay good money, there should be bread right??  The Owner was ever present, and FROM ITALY!
The vibe is really relaxed.
Food's  expensive.
We didn't mind the prices tho because fresh, quality ingredients are pricey. They have a mini deli to buy imported cheese and meat. That's cool. I would come back for the staff and the food. But I wouldn't travel for it.< /Text>
